2105         /**
2106          * Returns a ClassDefiner that creates a {@code Class} object of a hidden class
2107          * from the given bytes.  No package name check on the given name.
2108          *
2109          * @param name    fully-qualified name that specifies the prefix of the hidden class
2110          * @param bytes   class bytes
2111          * @return ClassDefiner that defines a hidden class of the given bytes.
2112          */
2113         ClassDefiner makeHiddenClassDefiner(String name, byte[] bytes) {
2114             return makeHiddenClassDefiner(name, bytes, Set.of(), false);
2115         }
2116 
2117         /**
2118          * Returns a ClassDefiner that creates a {@code Class} object of a hidden class
2119          * from the given bytes and options.  No package name check on the given name.
2120          *
2121          * @param name the name of the class and the name in the class bytes is ignored.
2122          * @param bytes class bytes
2123          * @param options class options
2124          * @param accessVmAnnotations true to give the hidden class access to VM annotations
2125          */
2126         ClassDefiner makeHiddenClassDefiner(String name,
2127                                             byte[] bytes,
2128                                             Set<ClassOption> options,
2129                                             boolean accessVmAnnotations) {
2130             int flags = HIDDEN_CLASS | ClassOption.optionsToFlag(options);
2131             if (accessVmAnnotations | VM.isSystemDomainLoader(lookupClass.getClassLoader())) {
2132                 // jdk.internal.vm.annotations are permitted for classes
2133                 // defined to boot loader and platform loader
2134                 flags |= ACCESS_VM_ANNOTATIONS;
2135             }
2136 
2137             return new ClassDefiner(this, name, bytes, flags);
2138         }
2139 
2140         static class ClassDefiner {
2141             private final Lookup lookup;
2142             private final String name;
2143             private final byte[] bytes;
2144             private final int classFlags;
2145 
2146             private ClassDefiner(Lookup lookup, String name, byte[] bytes, int flags) {
2147                 assert ((flags & HIDDEN_CLASS) != 0 || (flags & STRONG_LOADER_LINK) == STRONG_LOADER_LINK);
2148                 this.lookup = lookup;
2149                 this.bytes = bytes;
2150                 this.classFlags = flags;
2151                 this.name = name;
2152             }
2153 
2154             String className() {
2155                 return name;
2156             }
2157 
2158             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize) {
2159                 return defineClass(initialize, null);
2160             }
2161 
2162             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize) {
2163                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, null);
2164                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2165             }
2166 
2167             /**
2168              * Defines the class of the given bytes and the given classData.
2169              * If {@code initialize} parameter is true, then the class will be initialized.
2170              *
2171              * @param initialize true if the class to be initialized
2172              * @param classData classData or null
2173              * @return the class
2174              *
2175              * @throws LinkageError linkage error
2176              */
2177             Class<?> defineClass(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2178                 Class<?> lookupClass = lookup.lookupClass();
2179                 ClassLoader loader = lookupClass.getClassLoader();
2180                 ProtectionDomain pd = (loader != null) ? lookup.lookupClassProtectionDomain() : null;
2181                 Class<?> c = JLA.defineClass(loader, lookupClass, name, bytes, pd, initialize, classFlags, classData);
2182                 assert !isNestmate() || c.getNestHost() == lookupClass.getNestHost();
2183                 return c;
2184             }
2185 
2186             Lookup defineClassAsLookup(boolean initialize, Object classData) {
2187                 // initialize must be true if classData is non-null
2188                 assert classData == null || initialize == true;
2189                 Class<?> c = defineClass(initialize, classData);
2190                 return new Lookup(c, null, FULL_POWER_MODES);
2191             }
2192 
2193             private boolean isNestmate() {
2194                 return (classFlags & NESTMATE_CLASS) != 0;
2195             }
2196         }
2197 
2198         private ProtectionDomain lookupClassProtectionDomain() {
2199             ProtectionDomain pd = cachedProtectionDomain;
2200             if (pd == null) {
2201                 cachedProtectionDomain = pd = JLA.protectionDomain(lookupClass);
2202             }
2203             return pd;
2204         }
2205 
2206         // cached protection domain
2207         private volatile ProtectionDomain cachedProtectionDomain;
2208 
2209         // Make sure outer class is initialized first.
2210         static { IMPL_NAMES.getClass(); }
2211 
2212         /** Package-private version of lookup which is trusted. */
2213         static final Lookup IMPL_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, TRUSTED);
2214 
2215         /** Version of lookup which is trusted minimally.
2216          *  It can only be used to create method handles to publicly accessible
2217          *  members in packages that are exported unconditionally.
2218          */
2219         static final Lookup PUBLIC_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, UNCONDITIONAL);
2220 
2221         static final JavaLangAccess JLA = SharedSecrets.getJavaLangAccess();
2222 
2223         private static void checkUnprivilegedlookupClass(Class<?> lookupClass) {
2224             String name = lookupClass.getName();
2225             if (name.startsWith("java.lang.invoke."))
2226                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal lookupClass: "+lookupClass);
2227         }
2228 
2229         /**
2230          * Displays the name of the class from which lookups are to be made,
2231          * followed by "/" and the name of the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
2232          * previous lookup class} if present.
2233          * (The name is the one reported by {@link java.lang.Class#getName() Class.getName}.)
2234          * If there are restrictions on the access permitted to this lookup,
2235          * this is indicated by adding a suffix to the class name, consisting
2236          * of a slash and a keyword.  The keyword represents the strongest
2237          * allowed access, and is chosen as follows:
2238          * <ul>
2239          * <li>If no access is allowed, the suffix is "/noaccess".
2240          * <li>If only unconditional access is allowed, the suffix is "/publicLookup".
2241          * <li>If only public access to types in exported packages is allowed, the suffix is "/public".
2242          * <li>If only public and module access are allowed, the suffix is "/module".
2243          * <li>If public and package access are allowed, the suffix is "/package".
2244          * <li>If public, package, and private access are allowed, the suffix is "/private".
2245          * </ul>
2246          * If none of the above cases apply, it is the case that full access
2247          * (public, module, package, private, and protected) is allowed.
2248          * In this case, no suffix is added.
2249          * This is true only of an object obtained originally from
2250          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#lookup MethodHandles.lookup}.
2251          * Objects created by {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#in Lookup.in}
2252          * always have restricted access, and will display a suffix.
2253          * <p>
2254          * (It may seem strange that protected access should be
2255          * stronger than private access.  Viewed independently from
2256          * package access, protected access is the first to be lost,
2257          * because it requires a direct subclass relationship between
2258          * caller and callee.)
2259          * @see #in
2260          *
2261          * @revised 9
2262          * @spec JPMS
2263          */
2264         @Override
2265         public String toString() {
2266             String cname = lookupClass.getName();
2267             if (prevLookupClass != null)
2268                 cname += "/" + prevLookupClass.getName();
2269             switch (allowedModes) {
2270             case 0:  // no privileges
2271                 return cname + "/noaccess";
2272             case UNCONDITIONAL:
2273                 return cname + "/publicLookup";
2274             case PUBLIC:
2275                 return cname + "/public";
2276             case PUBLIC|MODULE:
2277                 return cname + "/module";
2278             case PUBLIC|PACKAGE:
2279             case PUBLIC|MODULE|PACKAGE:
2280                 return cname + "/package";
2281             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~PROTECTED):
2282             case FULL_POWER_MODES & ~(PROTECTED|MODULE):
2283                 return cname + "/private";
2284             case FULL_POWER_MODES:
2285             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~MODULE):
2286                 return cname;
2287             case TRUSTED:
2288                 return "/trusted";  // internal only; not exported
2289             default:  // Should not happen, but it's a bitfield...
2290                 cname = cname + "/" + Integer.toHexString(allowedModes);
2291                 assert(false) : cname;
2292                 return cname;
2293             }
2294         }
2295 
2296         /**
2297          * Produces a method handle for a static method.
2298          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method.
2299          * (Since static methods do not take receivers, there is no
2300          * additional receiver argument inserted into the method handle type,
2301          * as there would be with {@link #findVirtual findVirtual} or {@link #findSpecial findSpecial}.)
2302          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2303          * <p>
2304          * The returned method handle will have
2305          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2306          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2307          * <p>
2308          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
2309          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2310          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2311          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2312 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2313 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2314 ...
2315 MethodHandle MH_asList = publicLookup().findStatic(Arrays.class,
2316   "asList", methodType(List.class, Object[].class));
2317 assertEquals("[x, y]", MH_asList.invoke("x", "y").toString());
2318          * }</pre></blockquote>
2319          * @param refc the class from which the method is accessed
2320          * @param name the name of the method
2321          * @param type the type of the method
2322          * @return the desired method handle
2323          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2324          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2325          *                                or if the method is not {@code static},
2326          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2327          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2328          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2329          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2330          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2331          */
2332         public MethodHandle findStatic(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2333             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeStatic, refc, name, type);
2334             // resolveOrFail could return a non-static <init> method if present
2335             // detect and throw NSME before producing a MethodHandle
2336             if (!method.isStatic() && name.equals("<init>")) {
2337                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
2338             }
2339 
2340             return getDirectMethod(REF_invokeStatic, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2341         }
2342 
2343         /**
2344          * Produces a method handle for a virtual method.
2345          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2346          * with the receiver type (usually {@code refc}) prepended.
2347          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2348          * <p>
2349          * When called, the handle will treat the first argument as a receiver
2350          * and, for non-private methods, dispatch on the receiver's type to determine which method
2351          * implementation to enter.
2352          * For private methods the named method in {@code refc} will be invoked on the receiver.
2353          * (The dispatching action is identical with that performed by an
2354          * {@code invokevirtual} or {@code invokeinterface} instruction.)
2355          * <p>
2356          * The first argument will be of type {@code refc} if the lookup
2357          * class has full privileges to access the member.  Otherwise
2358          * the member must be {@code protected} and the first argument
2359          * will be restricted in type to the lookup class.
2360          * <p>
2361          * The returned method handle will have
2362          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2363          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2364          * <p>
2365          * Because of the general <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">equivalence</a> between {@code invokevirtual}
2366          * instructions and method handles produced by {@code findVirtual},
2367          * if the class is {@code MethodHandle} and the name string is
2368          * {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke}, the resulting
2369          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2370          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#exactInvoker MethodHandles.exactInvoker} or
2371          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#invoker MethodHandles.invoker}
2372          * with the same {@code type} argument.
2373          * <p>
2374          * If the class is {@code VarHandle} and the name string corresponds to
2375          * the name of a signature-polymorphic access mode method, the resulting
2376          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2377          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#varHandleInvoker} with
2378          * the access mode corresponding to the name string and with the same
2379          * {@code type} arguments.
2380          * <p>
2381          * <b>Example:</b>
2382          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2383 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2384 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2385 ...
2386 MethodHandle MH_concat = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2387   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
2388 MethodHandle MH_hashCode = publicLookup().findVirtual(Object.class,
2389   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2390 MethodHandle MH_hashCode_String = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2391   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2392 assertEquals("xy", (String) MH_concat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
2393 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode.invokeExact((Object)"xy"));
2394 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode_String.invokeExact("xy"));
2395 // interface method:
2396 MethodHandle MH_subSequence = publicLookup().findVirtual(CharSequence.class,
2397   "subSequence", methodType(CharSequence.class, int.class, int.class));
2398 assertEquals("def", MH_subSequence.invoke("abcdefghi", 3, 6).toString());
2399 // constructor "internal method" must be accessed differently:
2400 MethodType MT_newString = methodType(void.class); //()V for new String()
2401 try { assertEquals("impossible", lookup()
2402         .findVirtual(String.class, "<init>", MT_newString));
2403  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2404 MethodHandle MH_newString = publicLookup()
2405   .findConstructor(String.class, MT_newString);
2406 assertEquals("", (String) MH_newString.invokeExact());
2407          * }</pre></blockquote>
2408          *
2409          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2410          * @param name the name of the method
2411          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2412          * @return the desired method handle
2413          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2414          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2415          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2416          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2417          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2418          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2419          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2420          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2421          */
2422         public MethodHandle findVirtual(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2423             if (refc == MethodHandle.class) {
2424                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForMH(name, type);
2425                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2426             } else if (refc == VarHandle.class) {
2427                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForVH(name, type);
2428                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2429             }
2430             byte refKind = (refc.isInterface() ? REF_invokeInterface : REF_invokeVirtual);
2431             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(refKind, refc, name, type);
2432             return getDirectMethod(refKind, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2433         }
2434         private MethodHandle findVirtualForMH(String name, MethodType type) {
2435             // these names require special lookups because of the implicit MethodType argument
2436             if ("invoke".equals(name))
2437                 return invoker(type);
2438             if ("invokeExact".equals(name))
2439                 return exactInvoker(type);
2440             assert(!MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(name));
2441             return null;
2442         }
2443         private MethodHandle findVirtualForVH(String name, MethodType type) {
2444             try {
2445                 return varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode.valueFromMethodName(name), type);
2446             } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
2447                 return null;
2448             }
2449         }
2450 
2451         /**
2452          * Produces a method handle which creates an object and initializes it, using
2453          * the constructor of the specified type.
2454          * The parameter types of the method handle will be those of the constructor,
2455          * while the return type will be a reference to the constructor's class.
2456          * The constructor and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2457          * <p>
2458          * The requested type must have a return type of {@code void}.
2459          * (This is consistent with the JVM's treatment of constructor type descriptors.)
2460          * <p>
2461          * The returned method handle will have
2462          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2463          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2464          * <p>
2465          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
2466          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2467          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2468          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2469 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2470 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2471 ...
2472 MethodHandle MH_newArrayList = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2473   ArrayList.class, methodType(void.class, Collection.class));
2474 Collection orig = Arrays.asList("x", "y");
2475 Collection copy = (ArrayList) MH_newArrayList.invokeExact(orig);
2476 assert(orig != copy);
2477 assertEquals(orig, copy);
2478 // a variable-arity constructor:
2479 MethodHandle MH_newProcessBuilder = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2480   ProcessBuilder.class, methodType(void.class, String[].class));
2481 ProcessBuilder pb = (ProcessBuilder)
2482   MH_newProcessBuilder.invoke("x", "y", "z");
2483 assertEquals("[x, y, z]", pb.command().toString());
2484          * }</pre></blockquote>
2485          *
2486          * @apiNote
2487          * This method does not find a static {@code <init>} factory method as it is invoked
2488          * via {@code invokestatic} bytecode as opposed to {@code invokespecial} for an
2489          * object constructor.  To look up static {@code <init>} factory method, use
2490          * the {@link #findStatic(Class, String, MethodType) findStatic} method.
2491          *
2492          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2493          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted, and a void return type
2494          * @return the desired method handle
2495          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the constructor does not exist
2496          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
2497          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2498          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2499          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2500          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2501          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2502          */
2503         public MethodHandle findConstructor(Class<?> refc, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2504             if (refc.isArray()) {
2505                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("no constructor for array class: " + refc.getName());
2506             }
2507             if (type.returnType() != void.class) {
2508                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("Constructors must have void return type: " + refc.getName());
2509             }
2510             String name = "<init>";
2511             MemberName ctor = resolveOrFail(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2512             return getDirectConstructor(refc, ctor);
2513         }
2514 
2515         /**
2516          * Looks up a class by name from the lookup context defined by this {@code Lookup} object,
2517          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if resolved</a> by an {@code ldc} instruction.
2518          * Such a resolution, as specified in JVMS 5.4.3.1 section, attempts to locate and load the class,
2519          * and then determines whether the class is accessible to this lookup object.
2520          * <p>
2521          * The lookup context here is determined by the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class},
2522          * its class loader, and the {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes}.
2523          *
2524          * @param targetName the fully qualified name of the class to be looked up.
2525          * @return the requested class.
2526          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2527          *                           <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2528          * @throws LinkageError if the linkage fails
2529          * @throws ClassNotFoundException if the class cannot be loaded by the lookup class' loader.
2530          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible, using the allowed access
2531          * modes.
2532          * @since 9
2533          * @jvms 5.4.3.1 Class and Interface Resolution
2534          */
2535         public Class<?> findClass(String targetName) throws ClassNotFoundException, IllegalAccessException {
2536             Class<?> targetClass = Class.forName(targetName, false, lookupClass.getClassLoader());
2537             return accessClass(targetClass);
2538         }
2539 
2540         /**
2541          * Determines if a class can be accessed from the lookup context defined by
2542          * this {@code Lookup} object. The static initializer of the class is not run.
2543          * <p>
2544          * If the {@code targetClass} is in the same module as the lookup class,
2545          * the lookup class is {@code LC} in module {@code M1} and
2546          * the previous lookup class is in module {@code M0} or
2547          * {@code null} if not present,
2548          * {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if one of the following is true:
2549          * <ul>
2550          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PRIVATE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2551          *     {@code LC} or other class in the same nest of {@code LC}.</li>
2552          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PACKAGE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2553          *     in the same runtime package of {@code LC}.</li>
2554          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #MODULE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2555          *     a public type in {@code M1}.</li>
2556          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PUBLIC} access, {@code targetClass} is
2557          *     a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} to at least  {@code M0}
2558          *     if the previous lookup class is present; otherwise, {@code targetClass}
2559          *     is a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} unconditionally.</li>
2560          * </ul>
2561          *
2562          * <p>
2563          * Otherwise, if this lookup has {@link #UNCONDITIONAL} access, this lookup
2564          * can access public types in all modules when the type is in a package
2565          * that is exported unconditionally.
2566          * <p>
2567          * Otherwise, the target class is in a different module from {@code lookupClass},
2568          * and if this lookup does not have {@code PUBLIC} access, {@code lookupClass}
2569          * is inaccessible.
2570          * <p>
2571          * Otherwise, if this lookup has no {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2572          * {@code M1} is the module containing {@code lookupClass} and
2573          * {@code M2} is the module containing {@code targetClass},
2574          * then {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if
2575          * <ul>
2576          * <li>{@code M1} reads {@code M2}, and
2577          * <li>{@code targetClass} is public and in a package exported by
2578          *     {@code M2} at least to {@code M1}.
2579          * </ul>
2580          * <p>
2581          * Otherwise, if this lookup has a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2582          * {@code M1} and {@code M2} are as before, and {@code M0} is the module
2583          * containing the previous lookup class, then {@code targetClass} is accessible
2584          * if and only if one of the following is true:
2585          * <ul>
2586          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M0} and {@code M1}
2587          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M0} and the type is
2588          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M1}.
2589          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M1} and {@code M0}
2590          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M1} and the type is
2591          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M0}.
2592          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in a third module {@code M2} and both {@code M0}
2593          *     and {@code M1} reads {@code M2} and the type is in a package
2594          *     that is exported to at least both {@code M0} and {@code M2}.
2595          * </ul>
2596          * <p>
2597          * Otherwise, {@code targetClass} is not accessible.
2598          *
2599          * @param targetClass the class to be access-checked
2600          * @return the class that has been access-checked
2601          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible from the lookup class
2602          * and previous lookup class, if present, using the allowed access modes.
2603          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2604          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2605          * @since 9
2606          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
2607          */
2608         public Class<?> accessClass(Class<?> targetClass) throws IllegalAccessException {
2609             if (!VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(targetClass, lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
2610                 throw new MemberName(targetClass).makeAccessException("access violation", this);
2611             }
2612             checkSecurityManager(targetClass, null);
2613             return targetClass;
2614         }
2615 
2616         /**
2617          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a virtual method.
2618          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
2619          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
2620          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
2621          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2622          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
2623          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
2624          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible
2625          * to the lookup object.
2626          * <p>
2627          * Before method resolution,
2628          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
2629          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
2630          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
2631          * privileges, the access fails.
2632          * <p>
2633          * The returned method handle will have
2634          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2635          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2636          * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
2637          * <em>(Note:  JVM internal methods named {@code "<init>"} are not visible to this API,
2638          * even though the {@code invokespecial} instruction can refer to them
2639          * in special circumstances.  Use {@link #findConstructor findConstructor}
2640          * to access instance initialization methods in a safe manner.)</em>
2641          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2642          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2643 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2644 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2645 ...
2646 static class Listie extends ArrayList {
2647   public String toString() { return "[wee Listie]"; }
2648   static Lookup lookup() { return MethodHandles.lookup(); }
2649 }
2650 ...
2651 // no access to constructor via invokeSpecial:
2652 MethodHandle MH_newListie = Listie.lookup()
2653   .findConstructor(Listie.class, methodType(void.class));
2654 Listie l = (Listie) MH_newListie.invokeExact();
2655 try { assertEquals("impossible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2656         Listie.class, "<init>", methodType(void.class), Listie.class));
2657  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2658 // access to super and self methods via invokeSpecial:
2659 MethodHandle MH_super = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2660   ArrayList.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2661 MethodHandle MH_this = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2662   Listie.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2663 MethodHandle MH_duper = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2664   Object.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2665 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_super.invokeExact(l));
2666 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(l));
2667 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_duper.invokeExact(l)); // ArrayList method
2668 try { assertEquals("inaccessible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2669         String.class, "toString", methodType(String.class), Listie.class));
2670  } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) { } // OK
2671 Listie subl = new Listie() { public String toString() { return "[subclass]"; } };
2672 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(subl)); // Listie method
2673          * }</pre></blockquote>
2674          *
2675          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2676          * @param name the name of the method (which must not be "&lt;init&gt;")
2677          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2678          * @param specialCaller the proposed calling class to perform the {@code invokespecial}
2679          * @return the desired method handle
2680          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2681          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2682          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2683          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2684          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2685          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2686          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2687          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2688          */
2689         public MethodHandle findSpecial(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type,
2690                                         Class<?> specialCaller) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2691             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, refc);
2692             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
2693             MemberName method = specialLookup.resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2694             return specialLookup.getDirectMethod(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2695         }
2696 
2697         /**
2698          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a non-static field.
2699          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2700          * value type.
2701          * The method handle's single argument will be the instance containing
2702          * the field.
2703          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2704          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2705          * @param name the field's name
2706          * @param type the field's type
2707          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2708          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2709          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2710          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2711          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2712          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2713          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2714          */
2715         public MethodHandle findGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2716             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, refc, name, type);
2717             return getDirectField(REF_getField, refc, field);
2718         }
2719 
2720         /**
2721          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a non-static field.
2722          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2723          * The method handle will take two arguments, the instance containing
2724          * the field, and the value to be stored.
2725          * The second argument will be of the field's value type.
2726          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2727          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2728          * @param name the field's name
2729          * @param type the field's type
2730          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2731          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2732          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2733          *                                or {@code final}
2734          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2735          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2736          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2737          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2738          */
2739         public MethodHandle findSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2740             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, refc, name, type);
2741             return getDirectField(REF_putField, refc, field);
2742         }

2744         /**
2745          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a non-static field {@code name}
2746          * of type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code recv}.
2747          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has one
2748          * coordinate type, {@code recv}.
2749          * <p>
2750          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2751          * class.
2752          * <p>
2753          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2754          * the following conditions:
2755          * <ul>
2756          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2757          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2758          *     modes are unsupported.
2759          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2760          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2761          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
2762          *     access modes are unsupported.
2763          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2764          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2765          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2766          *     unsupported.
2767          * </ul>
2768          * <p>
2769          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2770          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2771          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2772          * access modes.
2773          * <p>
2774          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2775          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2776          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2777          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2778          * @apiNote
2779          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2780          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2781          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2782          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2783          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2784          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2785          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2786          * unexpectedly fail.
2787          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2788          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2789          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2790          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2791          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2792          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2793          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2794          * details).
2795          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2796          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2797          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2798          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2799          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2800          * @param recv the receiver class, of type {@code R}, that declares the
2801          * non-static field
2802          * @param name the field's name
2803          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2804          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields.
2805          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2806          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2807          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2808          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2809          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2810          * @since 9
2811          */
2812         public VarHandle findVarHandle(Class<?> recv, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2813             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, recv, name, type);
2814             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, recv, name, type);
2815             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getField, REF_putField, recv, getField, putField);
2816         }
2817 
2818         /**
2819          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a static field.
2820          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2821          * value type.
2822          * The method handle will take no arguments.
2823          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2824          * <p>
2825          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2826          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2827          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2828          * @param name the field's name
2829          * @param type the field's type
2830          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2831          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2832          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2833          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2834          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2835          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2836          */
2837         public MethodHandle findStaticGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2838             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, refc, name, type);
2839             return getDirectField(REF_getStatic, refc, field);
2840         }

2842         /**
2843          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a static field.
2844          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2845          * The method handle will take a single
2846          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
2847          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2848          * <p>
2849          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2850          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2851          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2852          * @param name the field's name
2853          * @param type the field's type
2854          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2855          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2856          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2857          *                                or is {@code final}
2858          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2859          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2860          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2861          */
2862         public MethodHandle findStaticSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2863             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, refc, name, type);
2864             return getDirectField(REF_putStatic, refc, field);
2865         }

2867         /**
2868          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a static field {@code name} of
2869          * type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code decl}.
2870          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has no
2871          * coordinate types.
2872          * <p>
2873          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2874          * class.
2875          * <p>
2876          * If the returned VarHandle is operated on, the declaring class will be
2877          * initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2878          * <p>
2879          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2880          * the following conditions:
2881          * <ul>
2882          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2883          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2884          *     modes are unsupported.
2885          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2886          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2887          *     {@code float}, or {@code double}, then numeric atomic update
2888          *     access modes are unsupported.
2889          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2890          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2891          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2892          *     unsupported.
2893          * </ul>
2894          * <p>
2895          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2896          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2897          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2898          * access modes.
2899          * <p>
2900          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2901          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2902          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2903          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2904          * @apiNote
2905          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2906          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2907          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2908          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2909          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2910          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2911          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2912          * unexpectedly fail.
2913          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2914          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2915          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2916          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2917          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2918          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2919          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2920          * details).
2921          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2922          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2923          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2924          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2925          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2926          * @param decl the class that declares the static field
2927          * @param name the field's name
2928          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2929          * @return a VarHandle giving access to a static field
2930          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2931          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2932          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2933          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2934          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2935          * @since 9
2936          */
2937         public VarHandle findStaticVarHandle(Class<?> decl, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2938             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, decl, name, type);
2939             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, decl, name, type);
2940             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getStatic, REF_putStatic, decl, getField, putField);
2941         }

2943         /**
2944          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a non-static method.
2945          * The receiver must have a supertype {@code defc} in which a method
2946          * of the given name and type is accessible to the lookup class.
2947          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2948          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2949          * without any insertion of an additional receiver parameter.
2950          * The given receiver will be bound into the method handle,
2951          * so that every call to the method handle will invoke the
2952          * requested method on the given receiver.
2953          * <p>
2954          * The returned method handle will have
2955          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2956          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set
2957          * <em>and</em> the trailing array argument is not the only argument.
2958          * (If the trailing array argument is the only argument,
2959          * the given receiver value will be bound to it.)
2960          * <p>
2961          * This is almost equivalent to the following code, with some differences noted below:
2962          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2963 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2964 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2965 ...
2966 MethodHandle mh0 = lookup().findVirtual(defc, name, type);
2967 MethodHandle mh1 = mh0.bindTo(receiver);
2968 mh1 = mh1.withVarargs(mh0.isVarargsCollector());
2969 return mh1;
2970          * }</pre></blockquote>
2971          * where {@code defc} is either {@code receiver.getClass()} or a super
2972          * type of that class, in which the requested method is accessible
2973          * to the lookup class.
2974          * (Unlike {@code bind}, {@code bindTo} does not preserve variable arity.
2975          * Also, {@code bindTo} may throw a {@code ClassCastException} in instances where {@code bind} would
2976          * throw an {@code IllegalAccessException}, as in the case where the member is {@code protected} and
2977          * the receiver is restricted by {@code findVirtual} to the lookup class.)
2978          * @param receiver the object from which the method is accessed
2979          * @param name the name of the method
2980          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2981          * @return the desired method handle
2982          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2983          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
2984          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2985          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2986          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2987          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2988          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2989          * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
2990          * @see #findVirtual
2991          */
2992         public MethodHandle bind(Object receiver, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2993             Class<? extends Object> refc = receiver.getClass(); // may get NPE
2994             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2995             MethodHandle mh = getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2996             if (!mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().isAssignableFrom(receiver.getClass())) {
2997                 throw new IllegalAccessException("The restricted defining class " +
2998                                                  mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().getName() +
2999                                                  " is not assignable from receiver class " +
3000                                                  receiver.getClass().getName());
3001             }
3002             return mh.bindArgumentL(0, receiver).setVarargs(method);
3003         }
3004 
3005         /**
3006          * Makes a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3007          * to <i>m</i>, if the lookup class has permission.
3008          * If <i>m</i> is non-static, the receiver argument is treated as an initial argument.
3009          * If <i>m</i> is virtual, overriding is respected on every call.
3010          * Unlike the Core Reflection API, exceptions are <em>not</em> wrapped.
3011          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3012          * with the receiver type prepended (but only if it is non-static).
3013          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3014          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3015          * If <i>m</i> is not public, do not share the resulting handle with untrusted parties.
3016          * <p>
3017          * The returned method handle will have
3018          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3019          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3020          * <p>
3021          * If <i>m</i> is static, and
3022          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
3023          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3024          * @param m the reflected method
3025          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3026          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3027          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3028          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3029          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3030          */
3031         public MethodHandle unreflect(Method m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3032             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == MethodHandle.class) {
3033                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForMH(m);
3034                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3035             }
3036             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == VarHandle.class) {
3037                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForVH(m);
3038                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3039             }
3040             MemberName method = new MemberName(m);
3041             byte refKind = method.getReferenceKind();
3042             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial)
3043                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3044             assert(method.isMethod());
3045             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3046             Lookup lookup = m.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3047             return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3048         }
3049         private MethodHandle unreflectForMH(Method m) {
3050             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3051             if (MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(m.getName()))
3052                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeMethodHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3053             return null;
3054         }
3055         private MethodHandle unreflectForVH(Method m) {
3056             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3057             if (MemberName.isVarHandleMethodInvokeName(m.getName()))
3058                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeVarHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3059             return null;
3060         }
3061 
3062         /**
3063          * Produces a method handle for a reflected method.
3064          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
3065          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
3066          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
3067          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3068          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
3069          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
3070          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3071          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class,
3072          * as if {@code invokespecial} instruction were being linked.
3073          * <p>
3074          * Before method resolution,
3075          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
3076          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
3077          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
3078          * privileges, the access fails.
3079          * <p>
3080          * The returned method handle will have
3081          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3082          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3083          * @param m the reflected method
3084          * @param specialCaller the class nominally calling the method
3085          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3086          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3087          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
3088          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3089          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3090          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3091          */
3092         public MethodHandle unreflectSpecial(Method m, Class<?> specialCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3093             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, m.getDeclaringClass());
3094             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
3095             MemberName method = new MemberName(m, true);
3096             assert(method.isMethod());
3097             // ignore m.isAccessible:  this is a new kind of access
3098             return specialLookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(REF_invokeSpecial, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3099         }
3100 
3101         /**
3102          * Produces a method handle for a reflected constructor.
3103          * The type of the method handle will be that of the constructor,
3104          * with the return type changed to the declaring class.
3105          * The method handle will perform a {@code newInstance} operation,
3106          * creating a new instance of the constructor's class on the
3107          * arguments passed to the method handle.
3108          * <p>
3109          * If the constructor's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3110          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3111          * <p>
3112          * The returned method handle will have
3113          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3114          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3115          * <p>
3116          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
3117          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3118          * @param c the reflected constructor
3119          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected constructor
3120          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3121          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3122          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3123          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3124          */
3125         public MethodHandle unreflectConstructor(Constructor<?> c) throws IllegalAccessException {
3126             MemberName ctor = new MemberName(c);
3127             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructorOrStaticInitMethod());
3128             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3129             Lookup lookup = c.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3130             if (ctor.isObjectConstructor()) {
3131                 assert(ctor.getReturnType() == void.class);
3132                 return lookup.getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor);
3133             } else {
3134                 // static init factory is a static method
3135                 assert(ctor.isMethod() && ctor.getReturnType() == ctor.getDeclaringClass() && ctor.getReferenceKind() == REF_invokeStatic);
3136                 assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // must not be caller-sensitive
3137                 return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(ctor.getReferenceKind(), ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor, lookup);
3138             }
3139         }
