3141         /**
3142          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a reflected field.
3143          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
3144          * value type.
3145          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take no arguments.
3146          * Otherwise, its single argument will be the instance containing
3147          * the field.
3148          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3149          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3150          * <p>
3151          * If the field is static, and
3152          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3153          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3154          * @param f the reflected field
3155          * @return a method handle which can load values from the reflected field
3156          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3157          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3158          */
3159         public MethodHandle unreflectGetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3160             return unreflectField(f, false);
3161         }
3162 
3163         /**
3164          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a reflected field.
3165          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3166          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take a single
3167          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
3168          * Otherwise, the two arguments will be the instance containing
3169          * the field, and the value to be stored.
3170          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3171          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3172          * <p>
3173          * If the field is {@code final}, write access will not be
3174          * allowed and access checking will fail, except under certain
3175          * narrow circumstances documented for {@link Field#set Field.set}.
3176          * A method handle is returned only if a corresponding call to
3177          * the {@code Field} object's {@code set} method could return
3178          * normally.  In particular, fields which are both {@code static}
3179          * and {@code final} may never be set.
3180          * <p>
3181          * If the field is {@code static}, and
3182          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3183          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3184          * @param f the reflected field
3185          * @return a method handle which can store values into the reflected field
3186          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3187          *         or if the field is {@code final} and write access
3188          *         is not enabled on the {@code Field} object
3189          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3190          */
3191         public MethodHandle unreflectSetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3192             return unreflectField(f, true);
3193         }
3194 
3195         private MethodHandle unreflectField(Field f, boolean isSetter) throws IllegalAccessException {
3196             MemberName field = new MemberName(f, isSetter);
3197             if (isSetter && field.isFinal()) {
3198                 if (field.isStatic()) {
3199                     throw field.makeAccessException("static final field has no write access", this);
3200                 } else if (field.getDeclaringClass().isHidden()){
3201                     throw field.makeAccessException("final field in a hidden class has no write access", this);
3202                 }
3203             }
3204             assert(isSetter
3205                     ? MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(field.getReferenceKind())
3206                     : MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(field.getReferenceKind()));
3207             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3208             Lookup lookup = f.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3209             return lookup.getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(field.getReferenceKind(), f.getDeclaringClass(), field);
3210         }
3211 
3212         /**
3213          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3214          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3215          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3216          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3217          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3218          * coordinate types.
3219          * <p>
3220          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3221          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3222          * flag.
3223          * <p>
3224          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3225          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3226          * already been initialized.
3227          * <p>
3228          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3229          * the following conditions:
3230          * <ul>
3231          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3232          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3233          *     modes are unsupported.
3234          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3235          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3236          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3237          *     access modes are unsupported.
3238          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3239          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3240          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3241          *     unsupported.
3242          * </ul>
3243          * <p>
3244          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3245          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3246          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3247          * access modes.
3248          * <p>
3249          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3250          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3251          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3252          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3253          * @apiNote
3254          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3255          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3256          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3257          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3258          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3259          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3260          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3261          * unexpectedly fail.
3262          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3263          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3264          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3265          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3266          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3267          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3268          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3269          * details).
3270          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3271          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3272          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3273          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3274          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3275          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3276          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3277          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3278          * field
3279          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3280          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3281          * @since 9
3282          */
3283         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3284             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3285             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3286             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3287                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3288         }
3289 
3290         /**
3291          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3292          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3293          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3294          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3295          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3296          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3297          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3298          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3299          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3300          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3301          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3302          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3303          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3304          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3305          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3306          * @since 1.8
3307          */
3308         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3309             if (!target.isCrackable()) {
3310                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3311             }
3312             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3313             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3314             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3315             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3316             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3317                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3318                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3319                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3320                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3321             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3322                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3323                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3324             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3325             try {
3326                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3327                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3328             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3329                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3330             }
3331             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3332                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3333                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3334                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3335             }
3336             // Produce the handle to the results.
3337             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3338         }
3339 
3340         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3341 
3342         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3343             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3344             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3345             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3346             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3347                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3348         }
3349 
3350         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3351             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3352             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3353             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3354             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3355             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3356                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3357         }
3358 
3359         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3360             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3361             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3362             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3363             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3364                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3365         }
3366 
3367         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3368             // do this before attempting to resolve
3369             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3370                 return null;
3371             }
3372             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3373             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3374             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3375         }
3376 
3377         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3378             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3379                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3380             }
3381         }
3382 
3383         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3384             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3385             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3386             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3387         }
3388 
3389         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3390         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3391             // "<init>" can only be invoked via invokespecial or it's a static init factory
3392             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial &&
3393                     !(refKind == REF_invokeStatic && name.equals("<init>"))) {
3394                     throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
3395             }
3396         }
3397 
3398         /**
3399          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3400          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3401          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3402          */
3403         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3404             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3405                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3406                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3407             }
3408             return this;
3409         }
3410 
3411         /**
3412          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3413          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3414          *
3415          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3416          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3417          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3418          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3419          * @since 9
3420          */
3421         @Deprecated(since="14")
3422         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3423             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3424         }
3425 
3426         /**
3427          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3428          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3429          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3430          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3431          *
3432          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3433          * @since 14
3434          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3435          */
3436         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3437             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3438         }
3439 
3440         /**
3441          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3442          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3443          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3444          */
3445         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3446             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3447 
3448             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3449             if (smgr == null)  return;
3450 
3451             // Step 1:
3452             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3453             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3454                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3455                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3456             }
3457 
3458             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3459                 // Step 2b:
3460                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3461                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3462                 }
3463                 return;
3464             }
3465 
3466             // Step 2a:
3467             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3468             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3469                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3470             }
3471 
3472             // Step 3:
3473             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3474             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3475                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3476             }
3477         }
3478 
3479         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3480             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3481             String message;
3482             if (m.isObjectConstructor())
3483                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3484             else if (!m.isMethod())
3485                 message = "expected a method";
3486             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3487                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3488             else
3489                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3490             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3491         }
3492 
3493         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3494             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3495             String message;
3496             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3497                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3498             else
3499                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3500             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3501         }
3502 
3503         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3504         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3505             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3506                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3507                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3508             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3509             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3510             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3511             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3512                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3513                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3514                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3515                     refc.isArray()) {
3516                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3517                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3518                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3519                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3520                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3521                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3522                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3523                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3524                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3525                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3526                 // requested array type.
3527                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3528                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3529                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3530             }
3531             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3532                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3533                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3534             }
3535             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3536                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3537                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3538             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3539             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3540                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3541                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3542                     return;
3543             } else {
3544                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3545                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3546                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3547                     return;
3548             }
3549             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3550         }
3551 
3552         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3553             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3554             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3555             // check the class first:
3556             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3557                                (defc == refc ||
3558                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3559             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3560                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3561                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3562                            (defc == refc ||
3563                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3564             }
3565             if (!classOK)
3566                 return "class is not public";
3567             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3568                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3569             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3570                 return "member is private";
3571             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3572                 return "member is protected";
3573             return "member is private to package";
3574         }
3575 
3576         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3577             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3578             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3579             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3580                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3581                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3582                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3583                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3584                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3585         }
3586 
3587         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3588             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3589             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3590             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3591                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3592                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3593                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3594                 return false;
3595             return true;
3596         }
3597         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3598             assert(!method.isStatic());
3599             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3600             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3601                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3602             }
3603             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3604             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3605             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3606             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3607             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3608             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3609         }
3610 
3611         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3612         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3613             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3614             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3615             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3616         }
3617         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3618         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3619             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3620             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3621             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3622         }
3623         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3624         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3625             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3626             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3627             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3628         }
3629         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3630         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3631                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3632                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3633                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3634             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3635             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3636             if (checkSecurity)
3637                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3638             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3639 
3640             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3641                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3642                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3643                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3644                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3645                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3646 
3647                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3648                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3649                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3650                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3651                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3652                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3653                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3654                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3655                 MemberName m2;
3656                 do {
3657                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3658                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3659                                         method.getName(),
3660                                         method.getMethodType(),
3661                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3662                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3663                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3664                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3665                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3666                 method = m2;
3667                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3668                 // redo basic checks
3669                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3670             }
3671             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3672             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3673             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3674             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3675                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3676                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3677             }
3678             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3679             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3680             return mh;
3681         }
3682         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3683                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3684             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3685                 return mh;
3686 
3687             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3688             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3689             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3690                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3691 
3692             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3693             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3694             return cbmh;
3695         }
3696 
3697         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3698         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3699             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3700             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3701         }
3702         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3703         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3704             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3705             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3706         }
3707         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3708         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3709                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3710             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3711             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3712             if (checkSecurity)
3713                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3714             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3715             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3716                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3717             if (doRestrict)
3718                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3719             return dmh;
3720         }
3721         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3722                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3723                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3724             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3725             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3726         }
3727         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3728                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3729                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3730             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3731             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3732         }
3733         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3734                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3735                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3736             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3737             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3738             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3739             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3740 
3741             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3742             if (checkSecurity)
3743                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3744 
3745             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3746                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3747                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3748                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3749                 // only required for non-final fields
3750                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3751                 if (checkSecurity)
3752                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3753             }
3754 
3755             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3756                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3757             if (doRestrict) {
3758                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3759                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3760                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3761                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3762                 }
3763                 refc = lookupClass();
3764             }
3765             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3766                                              this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.getDeclaringClass().isHidden());
3767         }
3768         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3769         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3770             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3771             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3772         }
3773         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3774         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3775             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3776             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3777         }
3778         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3779         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3780                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3781             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructor());
3782             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3783             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3784             if (checkSecurity)
3785                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3786             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3787             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3788         }
3789 
3790         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3791          */
3792         /*non-public*/
3793         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3794                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3795             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3796                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3797             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3798             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3799             if (mh != null) {
3800                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3801                 return mh;
3802             }
3803             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3804                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3805                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3806                 if (mh != null) {
3807                     return mh;
3808                 }
3809             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3810                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3811                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3812                 if (mh != null) {
3813                     return mh;
3814                 }
3815             }
3816             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3817             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3818             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3819                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3820                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3821                 if (key != null) {
3822                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3823                 }
3824                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3825                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3826                 }
3827             }
3828             return mh;
3829         }
3830         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3831             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3832                 return false;
3833             }
3834             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3835                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3836                     !member.isPublic() ||
3837                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3838                 return false;
3839             }
3840             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3841             if (loader != null) {
3842                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3843                 boolean found = false;
3844                 while (sysl != null) {
3845                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3846                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3847                 }
3848                 if (!found) {
3849                     return false;
3850                 }
3851             }
3852             try {
3853                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3854                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3855                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3856                     return false;
3857                 }
3858                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3859             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3860                 return false;
3861             }
3862             return true;
3863         }
3864         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3865                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3866             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3867                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3868             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3869                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3870             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3871                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3872             }
3873             // oops
3874             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3875         }
3876 
3877         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3878     }
3879 
3880     /**
3881      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3882      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3883      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3884      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3885      *
3886      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3887      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3888      *
3889      * @param arrayClass an array type
3890      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3891      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3892      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3893      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3894      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3895      * @since 9
3896      */
3897     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3898         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
3899             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
3900         }
3901         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
3902                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
3903         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
3904     }
3905 
3906     /**
3907      * Produces a method handle returning the length of an array,
3908      * as if by the {@code arraylength} bytecode.
3909      * The type of the method handle will have {@code int} as return type,
3910      * and its sole argument will be the array type.
3911      *
3912      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a {@code null}
3913      * array reference, a {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown.
3914      *
3915      * @param arrayClass an array type
3916      * @return a method handle which can retrieve the length of an array of the given array type
3917      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3918      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3919      * @jvms 6.5 {@code arraylength} Instruction
3920      * @since 9
3921      */
3922     public static MethodHandle arrayLength(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3923         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.LENGTH);
3924     }

3926     /**
3927      * Produces a method handle giving read access to elements of an array,
3928      * as if by the {@code aaload} bytecode.
3929      * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the array's
3930      * element type.  Its first argument will be the array type,
3931      * and the second will be {@code int}.
3932      *
3933      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3934      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3935      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3936      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3937      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3938      * the length of the array.
3939      *
3940      * @param arrayClass an array type
3941      * @return a method handle which can load values from the given array type
3942      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3943      * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3944      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aaload} Instruction
3945      */
3946     public static MethodHandle arrayElementGetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3947         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.GET);
3948     }
3949 
3950     /**
3951      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3952      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3953      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3954      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3955      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3956      *
3957      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3958      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3959      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3960      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3961      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3962      * the length of the array.
3963      *
3964      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
3965      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
3966      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3967      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3968      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
3969      */
3970     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3971         if (arrayClass.isInlineClass()) {
3972             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
3973         }
3974         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
3975     }
3976 
3977     /**
3978      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
3979      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
3980      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3981      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3982      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
3983      * <p>
3984      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3985      * the following conditions:
3986      * <ul>
3987      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
3988      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3989      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
3990      *     modes are unsupported.
3991      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3992      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3993      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3994      *     unsupported.
3995      * </ul>
3996      * <p>
3997      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3998      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3999      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4000      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4001      *
4002      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4003      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4004      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4005      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4006      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4007      * the length of the array.
4008      *
4009      * @apiNote
4010      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4011      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4012      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4013      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4014      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4015      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4016      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4017      * unexpectedly fail.
4018      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4019      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4020      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4021      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4022      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4023      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4024      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4025      * details).
4026      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4027      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4028      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4029      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4030      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4031      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4032      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4033      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4034      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4035      * @since 9
4036      */
4037     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4038         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4039     }
4040 
4041     /**
4042      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4043      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4044      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4045      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4046      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4047      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4048      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4049      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4050      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4051      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4052      * <p>
4053      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4054      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4055      * {@code double}.
4056      * <p>
4057      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4058      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4059      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4060      * of {@code T}.
4061      * <p>
4062      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4063      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4064      * with the array and index.
4065      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4066      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4067      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4068      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4069      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4070      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4071      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4072      * <ul>
4073      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4074      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4075      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4076      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4077      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4078      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4079      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4080      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4081      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4082      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4083      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4084      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4085      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4086      * </ul>
4087      * <p>
4088      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4089      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4090      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4091      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4092      * <pre>{@code
4093      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4094      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4095      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4096      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4097      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4098      * }</pre>
4099      * <p>
4100      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4101      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4102      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4103      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4104      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4105      * type {@code T}
4106      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4107      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4108      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4109      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4110      * array class
4111      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4112      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4113      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4114      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4115      * @since 9
4116      */
4117     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4118                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4119         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4120         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4121                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4122     }
4123 
4124     /**
4125      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4126      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4127      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4128      * {@code long[]}.
4129      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4130      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4131      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4132      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4133      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4134      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4135      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4136      * <p>
4137      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4138      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4139      * {@code double}.
4140      * <p>
4141      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4142      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4143      * <p>
4144      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4145      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4146      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4147      * {@code T}.
4148      * <p>
4149      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4150      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4151      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4152      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4153      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4154      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4155      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4156      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4157      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4158      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4159      * <ul>
4160      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4161      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4162      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4163      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4164      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4165      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4166      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4167      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4168      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4169      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4170      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4171      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4172      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4173      * </ul>
4174      * <p>
4175      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4176      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4177      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4178      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4179      * <pre>{@code
4180      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4181      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4182      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4183      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4184      * }</pre>
4185      * <p>
4186      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4187      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4188      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4189      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4190      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4191      * type {@code T}
4192      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4193      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4194      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4195      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4196      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4197      * array class
4198      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4199      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4200      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4201      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4202      * @since 9
4203      */
4204     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4205                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4206         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4207         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4208                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4209     }

4211 
4212     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4213 
4214     /**
4215      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4216      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4217      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4218      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4219      * arguments:
4220      * <ul>
4221      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4222      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4223      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4224      * </ul>
4225      * <p>
4226      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4227      * the indicated {@code type}.
4228      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4229      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4230      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4231      * <p>
4232      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4233      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4234      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4235      * the final parameter.
4236      * <p>
4237      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4238      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4239      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4240      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4241      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4242      * <p>
4243      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4244      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4245 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4246 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4247 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4248 return invoker;
4249      * }</pre></blockquote>
4250      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4251      * @param type the desired target type
4252      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4253      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4254      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4255      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4256      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4257      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4258      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4259      */
4260     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4261         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4262             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4263         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4264         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4265     }
4266 
4267     /**
4268      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4269      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4270      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4271      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4272      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4273      * <p>
4274      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4275      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4276      *
4277      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4278      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4279      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4280      * of unknown types.
4281      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4282      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4283      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4284      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4285      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4286      * is unknown.)
4287      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4288      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4289      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4290      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4291      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4292      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4293      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4294      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4295      * <p>
4296      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4297      * @param type the desired target type
4298      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4299      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4300      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4301      */
4302     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4303         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4304     }
4305 
4306     /**
4307      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4308      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4309      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4310      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4311      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4312      * <p>
4313      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4314      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4315      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4316      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4317      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4318      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4319      * <p>
4320      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4321      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4322      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4323      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4324      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4325      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4326      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4327      * of the same arity as the general type.
4328      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4329      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4330      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4331      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4332      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4333      * <p>
4334      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4335      * @param type the desired target type
4336      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4337      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4338      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4339      */
4340     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4341         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4342     }

4358     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {

4394 
4395      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4396 
4397     /**
4398      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4399      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4400      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4401      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4402      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4403      * <p>
4404      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4405      * <p>
4406      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4407      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4408      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4409      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4410      * <ul>
4411      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4412      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4413      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4414      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4415      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4416      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4417      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4418      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4419      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4420      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4421      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4422      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4423      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4424      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4425      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4426      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4427      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4428      *     the low-order bit.
4429      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4430      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4431      * </ul>
4432      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4433      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4434      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4435      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4436      *           necessary return value conversions
4437      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4438      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4439      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4440      */
4441     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4442         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4443         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4444         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4445         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4446         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4447             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4448         }
4449         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4450     }
4451 
4452     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4453         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4454             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4455         }
4456     }
4457 
4458     /**
4459      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4460      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4461      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4462      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4463      * <p>
4464      * The given array controls the reordering.
4465      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4466      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4467      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4468      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4469      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4470      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4471      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4472      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4473      * <p>
4474      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4475      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4476      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4477      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4478      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4479      * type of the original target.
4480      * <p>
4481      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4482      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4483      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4484      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4485      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4486      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4487      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4488      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4489 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4490 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4491 ...
4492 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4493 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4494 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4495 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4496 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4497 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4498 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4499 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4500 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4501 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4502 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4503 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4504      * }</pre></blockquote>
4505      * <p>
4506      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4507      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
