7102      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7103      * }</pre></blockquote>
7104      *
7105      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7106      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7107      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7108      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7109      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7110      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7111      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7112      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7113      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7114      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7115      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7116      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7117      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7118      *     }
7119      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7120      *     MethodHandle[]
7121      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7122      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7123      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7124      * }
7125      * }</pre></blockquote>
7126      *
7127      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7128      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7129      *                 See above for other constraints.
7130      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7131      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7132      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7133      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7134      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7135      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7136      *             See above for other constraints.
7137      *
7138      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7139      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7140      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7141      *
7142      * @since 9
7143      */
7144     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7145         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7146         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7147         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7148         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7149         MethodHandle startIter;
7150         MethodHandle nextVal;
7151         {
7152             MethodType iteratorType;
7153             if (iterator == null) {
7154                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7155                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7156                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7157             } else {
7158                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7159                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7160                 startIter = iterator;
7161             }
7162             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7163             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7164 
7165             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7166             try {
7167                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7168                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7169             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7170                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7171             }
7172         }
7173 
7174         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7175         if (returnType != void.class) {
7176             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7177             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7178             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7179             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7180         }
7181 
7182         MethodHandle[]
7183             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7184             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7185         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7186     }
7187 
7188     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7189         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7190         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7191         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7192         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7193         // strip leading V value if present
7194         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7195         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7196             // argument list has no "V" => error
7197             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7198             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7199         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7200             // missing T type => error
7201             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7202             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7203         }
7204         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7205         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7206         if (iterator != null) {
7207             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7208             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7209             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7210                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7211             }
7212             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7213             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7214                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7215             }
7216             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7217                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7218                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7219             }
7220         } else {
7221             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7222                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7223                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7224                 // of Iterable
7225                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7226                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7227             } else {
7228                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7229                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7230                 // assignable to Iterable
7231                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7232                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7233                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7234                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7235                 }
7236             }
7237         }
7238         if (init != null) {
7239             MethodType initType = init.type();
7240             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7241                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7242                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7243             }
7244         }
7245         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7246     }
7247 
7248     /*non-public*/
7249     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7250         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7251         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7252         int[] order = new int[arity];
7253         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7254         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7255         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7256         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7257         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7258         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7259     }
7260 
7261     /**
7262      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7263      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7264      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7265      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7266      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7267      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7268      * <p>
7269      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7270      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7271      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7272      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7273      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7274      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7275      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7276      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7277      * <p>
7278      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7279      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7280      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7281      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7282      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7283      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7284      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7285      * </ul>
7286      * <p>
7287      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7288      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7289      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7290      * the cleanup.
7291      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7292      * V target(A..., B...);
7293      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7294      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7295      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7296      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7297      *   try {
7298      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7299      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7300      *     throwable = t;
7301      *     throw t;
7302      *   } finally {
7303      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7304      *   }
7305      *   return result;
7306      * }
7307      * }</pre></blockquote>
7308      * <p>
7309      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7310      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7311      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7312      * <p>
7313      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7314      * always throws.
7315      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7316      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7317      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7318      * <p>
7319      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7320      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7321      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7322      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7323      * <p>
7324      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7325      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7326      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7327      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7328      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7329      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7330      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7331      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7332      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7333      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7334      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7335      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7336      *
7337      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7338      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7339      *
7340      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7341      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7342      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7343      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7344      *          not match in their return types and their
7345      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7346      *
7347      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7348      * @since 9
7349      */
7350     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7351         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7352         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7353 
7354         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7355 
7356         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7357         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7358         // target parameter list.
7359         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7360 
7361         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7362         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7363         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7364 
7365         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7366         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7367     }
7368 
7369     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7370         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7371         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7372             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7373         }
7374         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7375         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7376             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7377         }
7378         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7379             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7380         }
7381         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7382         // target parameter list.
7383         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7384         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7385             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7386                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7387         }
7388     }
7389 
7390 }
